{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_RQVudcFmqtjssY6JlRRfNwKE","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Pipeline Specification Reference\n     2→\n     3→Loaded during Phase 2 of portification. This ref provides the detailed specification patterns for converting a workflow analysis into concrete code designs.\n     4→\n     5→## Step Graph Design\n     6→\n     7→### Step Definition Pattern\n     8→\n     9→Every workflow operation that produces an artifact maps to a `Step`:\n    10→\n    11→```python\n    12→Step(\n    13→    id=\"step-id\",              # kebab-case, unique within pipeline\n    14→    prompt=build_X_prompt(),   # Function from prompts.py\n    15→    output_file=\"artifact.md\", # Relative to work_dir\n    16→    gate=STEP_GATE,            # From gates.py\n    17→    gate_mode=GateMode.BLOCKING,  # BLOCKING (default) or TRAILING\n    18→    timeout_seconds=600,       # Per-step timeout\n    19→    inputs=[\"dep1.md\"],        # Files this step reads\n    20→    retry_limit=1,             # How many retries on gate failure\n    21→    model=None,                # None = use default from config\n    22→)\n    23→```\n    24→\n    25→### Gate Mode Selection\n    26→\n    27→Choose `GateMode` based on step criticality:\n    28→- `BLOCKING` (default): Pipeline halts if gate fails. Use for steps whose output is consumed by downstream steps.\n    29→- `TRAILING`: Gate evaluates asynchronously; pipeline continues. Use for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n    30→\n    31→Rule of thumb from `resolve_gate_mode()`:\n    32→- Release scope → always BLOCKING\n    33→- Milestone scope → configurable\n    34→- Task scope → TRAILING when `grace_period > 0`\n    35→\n    36→### Parallel Group Pattern\n    37→\n    38→Steps that can run concurrently are wrapped in a list:\n    39→\n    40→```python\n    41→steps = [\n    42→    single_step_1,\n    43→    [parallel_step_a, parallel_step_b],  # Run concurrently\n    44→    single_step_2,                        # Waits for parallel group\n    45→]\n    46→```\n    47→\n    48→The generic `execute_pipeline()` handles thread coordination. If using sprint-style custom executor, implement your own parallel dispatch.\n    49→\n    50→### Dependency Rules\n    51→\n    52→- Steps consume outputs of prior steps via `inputs` list\n    53→- A step can only reference outputs from steps that precede it in the graph\n    54→- Parallel steps within a group must not depend on each other\n    55→- Resume logic skips steps whose output already passes their gate\n    56→\n    57→## Model Design Patterns\n    58→\n    59→### Config Model\n    60→\n    61→Always extend `PipelineConfig`:\n    62→\n    63→```python\n    64→@dataclass\n    65→class MyConfig(PipelineConfig):\n    66→    \"\"\"Pipeline-specific configuration.\"\"\"\n    67→    # Required: identify the input\n    68→    source_path: Path\n    69→\n    70→    # Optional: control behavior\n    71→    depth: str = \"standard\"       # quick|standard|deep\n    72→\n    73→    # Computed paths\n    74→    @property\n    75→    def results_dir(self) -> Path:\n    76→        return self.work_dir / \"results\"\n    77→\n    78→    @property\n    79→    def output_file(self, step_id: str) -> Path:\n    80→        return self.work_dir / f\"{step_id}-output.md\"\n    81→```\n    82→\n    83→### Status Enum\n    84→\n    85→Sprint-style pipelines need richer status than generic `StepStatus`:\n    86→\n    87→```python\n    88→class StepPhaseStatus(Enum):\n    89→    PENDING = \"pending\"\n    90→    RUNNING = \"running\"\n    91→    PASS = \"pass\"\n    92→    PASS_NO_SIGNAL = \"pass_no_signal\"    # Completed but no structured report\n    93→    PASS_NO_REPORT = \"pass_no_report\"    # Output exists but no result file\n    94→    INCOMPLETE = \"incomplete\"             # Budget exhausted\n    95→    HALT = \"halt\"                         # Step recommends stopping\n    96→    TIMEOUT = \"timeout\"                   # Hard timeout exceeded\n    97→    ERROR = \"error\"                       # Process crash\n    98→    SKIPPED = \"skipped\"                   # Skipped by config\n    99→```\n   100→\n   101→### Result Model\n   102→\n   103→Extend `StepResult` with domain telemetry:\n   104→\n   105→```python\n   106→@dataclass\n   107→class MyStepResult(StepResult):\n   108→    exit_code: int | None = None\n   109→    started_at: float | None = None\n   110→    finished_at: float | None = None\n   111→    output_bytes: int = 0\n   112→    error_bytes: int = 0\n   113→    # Domain-specific fields:\n   114→    artifacts_produced: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)\n   115→    gate_details: dict = field(default_factory=dict)\n   116→```\n   117→\n   118→### Monitor State\n   119→\n   120→Domain-specific signals extracted from NDJSON output:\n   121→\n   122→```python\n   123→@dataclass\n   124→class MyMonitorState:\n   125→    output_bytes: int = 0\n   126→    last_growth_time: float = 0.0\n   127→    events_received: int = 0\n   128→    lines_total: int = 0\n   129→    growth_rate_bps: float = 0.0\n   130→    stall_seconds: float = 0.0\n   131→    # Domain-specific signals:\n   132→    last_step_id: str | None = None\n   133→    current_artifact: str | None = None\n   134→    files_changed: set = field(default_factory=set)\n   135→```\n   136→\n   137→## Gate Design Patterns\n   138→\n   139→### Gate Criteria Tiers\n   140→\n   141→```python\n   142→# Exempt: always passes (for optional/informational steps)\n   143→EXEMPT_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   144→    required_frontmatter_fields=[],\n   145→    min_lines=0,\n   146→    enforcement_tier=\"EXEMPT\",\n   147→)\n   148→\n   149→# Light: file exists and non-empty\n   150→LIGHT_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   151→    required_frontmatter_fields=[],\n   152→    min_lines=0,\n   153→    enforcement_tier=\"LIGHT\",\n   154→)\n   155→\n   156→# Standard: structural validation\n   157→STANDARD_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   158→    required_frontmatter_fields=[\"title\", \"status\"],\n   159→    min_lines=50,\n   160→    enforcement_tier=\"STANDARD\",\n   161→)\n   162→\n   163→# Strict: structural + semantic validation\n   164→STRICT_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   165→    required_frontmatter_fields=[\"title\", \"status\", \"convergence_score\"],\n   166→    min_lines=100,\n   167→    enforcement_tier=\"STRICT\",\n   168→    semantic_checks=[\n   169→        SemanticCheck(\n   170→            name=\"no_heading_gaps\",\n   171→            check_fn=_no_heading_gaps,\n   172→            failure_message=\"Heading hierarchy has gaps (e.g. H1→H3 without H2)\",\n   173→        ),\n   174→        SemanticCheck(\n   175→            name=\"refs_resolve\",\n   176→            check_fn=_cross_refs_resolve,\n   177→            failure_message=\"Cross-references do not resolve to valid targets\",\n   178→        ),\n   179→    ],\n   180→)\n   181→```\n   182→\n   183→### Semantic Check Functions\n   184→\n   185→Semantic checks are pure functions matching the `Callable[[str], bool]` signature — they take file content and return a boolean:\n   186→\n   187→```python\n   188→def _no_heading_gaps(content: str) -> bool:\n   189→    \"\"\"Verify heading hierarchy has no gaps (H1->H3 without H2).\"\"\"\n   190→    # ... implementation ...\n   191→    return True  # or False on failure\n   192→\n   193→def _has_required_sections(content: str) -> bool:\n   194→    \"\"\"Verify all required sections are present.\"\"\"\n   195→    required = {\"## Summary\", \"## Findings\", \"## Recommendations\"}\n   196→    present = {line.strip() for line in content.splitlines() if line.startswith(\"## \")}\n   197→    missing = required - present\n   198→    return len(missing) == 0\n   199→```\n   200→\n   201→### Frontmatter Validation\n   202→\n   203→The shared `gate_passed()` function handles YAML frontmatter checks. Steps that produce markdown with frontmatter get automatic validation:\n   204→\n   205→```yaml\n   206→---\n   207→title: Diff Analysis\n   208→status: complete\n   209→diff_points: 12\n   210→convergence_ready: true\n   211→---\n   212→```\n   213→\n   214→## Prompt Design Patterns\n   215→\n   216→### Prompt Builder Structure\n   217→\n   218→Each step's prompt is a function that takes inputs and returns a complete prompt string:\n   219→\n   220→```python\n   221→def build_analysis_prompt(source_path: Path, config: MyConfig) -> str:\n   222→    return f\"\"\"Read the source file and produce a structured analysis.\n   223→\n   224→Source: {source_path}\n   225→Depth: {config.depth}\n   226→\n   227→## Required Output Format\n   228→\n   229→Write your analysis to the output file with this structure:\n   230→\n   231→```yaml\n   232→---\n   233→title: Analysis Report\n   234→status: complete\n   235→finding_count: <integer>\n   236→---\n   237→```\n   238→\n   239→## Sections Required\n   240→\n   241→### Summary\n   242→Brief overview of findings.\n   243→\n   244→### Findings\n   245→Numbered list of findings with evidence.\n   246→\n   247→### Recommendations\n   248→Actionable next steps.\n   249→\n   250→## Machine-Readable Markers\n   251→\n   252→At the end of your output, include:\n   253→```\n   254→EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE\n   255→```\n   256→or\n   257→```\n   258→EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: HALT\n   259→```\n   260→\"\"\"\n   261→```\n   262→\n   263→### Key Prompt Rules\n   264→\n   265→1. **Specify output file format** — Tell Claude exactly what frontmatter fields to include\n   266→2. **Require machine-readable markers** — `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT` for status determination\n   267→3. **Embed input content when small** — Under ~50KB, embed directly in prompt; otherwise use `--file` args\n   268→4. **Be explicit about sections** — Name every required section; don't leave structure to inference\n   269→5. **Include depth/focus constraints** — If the step has configurable depth, encode it in the prompt\n   270→\n   271→### Input Embedding Pattern\n   272→\n   273→```python\n   274→def _embed_inputs(prompt: str, inputs: list[Path], config: MyConfig) -> tuple[str, list[str]]:\n   275→    \"\"\"Embed small input files directly into prompt, return file args for large ones.\"\"\"\n   276→    file_args = []\n   277→    for input_path in inputs:\n   278→        full_path = config.work_dir / input_path\n   279→        if full_path.stat().st_size < 50_000:\n   280→            content = full_path.read_text()\n   281→            prompt += f\"\\n\\n---\\n## Input: {input_path}\\n\\n{content}\"\n   282→        else:\n   283→            file_args.append(str(full_path))\n   284→    return prompt, file_args\n   285→```\n   286→\n   287→## Executor Design Patterns\n   288→\n   289→### Sprint-Style Supervisor Loop\n   290→\n   291→The sprint executor pattern provides supervised execution with monitoring. IMPORTANT: Sprint uses synchronous execution with `threading` for parallelism, NOT `async/await`. Use `time.sleep()` polling loops and `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch dispatch.\n   292→\n   293→```python\n   294→def execute_pipeline(config: MyConfig) -> MyResult:\n   295→    # 1. Pre-flight checks\n   296→    verify_claude_binary()\n   297→\n   298→    # 2. Setup infrastructure\n   299→    signal_handler = SignalHandler()\n   300→    logger = MyLogger(config)\n   301→    tui = MyTUI(config)\n   302→    monitor = OutputMonitor()\n   303→    result = MyResult(config=config)\n   304→    ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=config.max_turns)\n   305→\n   306→    # 3. Start TUI\n   307→    tui.start()\n   308→\n   309→    try:\n   310→        for step in config.steps:\n   311→            if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   312→                break\n   313→\n   314→            # 4. Reset monitor for this step\n   315→            monitor.reset(config.output_file(step))\n   316→            monitor.start()\n   317→\n   318→            # 5. Launch Claude subprocess\n   319→            process = ClaudeProcess(config, step)\n   320→            process.start()\n   321→\n   322→            # 6. Supervision loop\n   323→            while process.is_running():\n   324→                if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   325→                    process.stop()\n   326→                    break\n   327→\n   328→                state = monitor.get_state()\n   329→\n   330→                # Stall detection\n   331→                if state.stall_seconds > config.stall_timeout:\n   332→                    process.stop()\n   333→                    break\n   334→\n   335→                # TUI update\n   336→                tui.update(step, state)\n   337→                time.sleep(0.5)\n   338→\n   339→            # 7. Classify result\n   340→            monitor.stop()\n   341→            status = determine_status(process.exit_code, step, config)\n   342→\n   343→            # 8. Record and decide\n   344→            step_result = build_result(step, status, monitor.state)\n   345→            result.add(step_result)\n   346→            logger.write_step_result(step_result)\n   347→\n   348→            if status not in (PASS, PASS_NO_SIGNAL):\n   349→                # Collect diagnostics and halt\n   350→                diagnostics = collect_diagnostics(step_result, monitor.state)\n   351→                write_diagnostic_report(diagnostics, config)\n   352→                result.outcome = HALTED\n   353→                break\n   354→\n   355→    finally:\n   356→        tui.stop()\n   357→        monitor.stop()\n   358→        signal_handler.restore()\n   359→\n   360→    return result\n   361→```\n   362→\n   363→### Status Classification\n   364→\n   365→Map every possible exit condition to a deterministic status:\n   366→\n   367→```python\n   368→def determine_status(exit_code, step, config):\n   369→    # 1. Hard failures\n   370→    if exit_code == 124:\n   371→        return TIMEOUT\n   372→    if exit_code != 0:\n   373→        return ERROR\n   374→\n   375→    # 2. Check for structured result file\n   376→    result_path = config.result_file(step)\n   377→    if result_path.exists():\n   378→        content = result_path.read_text()\n   379→        if \"EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: HALT\" in content:\n   380→            return HALT\n   381→        if \"EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE\" in content:\n   382→            return PASS\n   383→        return PASS_NO_SIGNAL\n   384→\n   385→    # 3. Check for output without result\n   386→    output_path = config.output_file(step)\n   387→    if output_path.exists():\n   388→        if detect_error_max_turns(output_path):\n   389→            return INCOMPLETE\n   390→        return PASS_NO_REPORT\n   391→\n   392→    # 4. No output at all\n   393→    return ERROR\n   394→```\n   395→\n   396→## Integration Patterns\n   397→\n   398→### main.py Registration\n   399→\n   400→```python\n   401→# In src/superclaude/cli/main.py\n   402→from superclaude.cli.my_pipeline import my_pipeline_group\n   403→app.add_command(my_pipeline_group)\n   404→```\n   405→\n   406→### Click Command Group\n   407→\n   408→```python\n   409→@click.group(\"my-pipeline\")\n   410→def my_pipeline_group():\n   411→    \"\"\"My pipeline description.\"\"\"\n   412→    pass\n   413→\n is_flag=True)\n   421→def run(source, depth, dry_run, max_turns, model, debug):\n   422→    \"\"\"Execute the pipeline.\"\"\"\n   423→    config = load_config(source, depth=depth, dry_run=dry_run, ...)\n   424→    result = execute_pipeline(config)\n   425→    sys.exit(0 if result.success else 1)\n   426→```\n   427→\n   428→## Turn Budget Economics (from unified-audit-gating)\n   429→\n   430→For pipelines with multiple Claude subprocesses, use `TurnLedger` to manage budget:\n   431→\n   432→```python\n   433→from superclaude.cli.sprint.models import TurnLedger\n   434→\n   435→@dataclass\n   436→class MyConfig(PipelineConfig):\n   437→    max_turns: int = 200\n   438→    min_launch_allocation: int = 10\n   439→    min_remediation_budget: int = 5\n   440→\n   441→# In executor:\n   442→ledger = TurnLedger(\n   443→    initial_budget=config.max_turns,\n   444→    minimum_allocation=config.min_launch_allocation,\n   445→    minimum_remediation_budget=config.min_remediation_budget,\n   446→)\n   447→\n   448→# Before launching a step:\n   449→if not ledger.can_launch():\n   450→    result.outcome = HALTED\n   451→    result.halt_reason = \"Budget exhausted\"\n   452→    break\n   453→\n   454→# After step completes, count actual turns used:\n   455→actual_turns = count_turns_from_output(output_path)\n   456→ledger.debit(actual_turns)\n   457→\n   458→# If step used fewer turns than allocated, credit back:\n   459→if actual_turns < allocated:\n   460→    ledger.credit(allocated - actual_turns)\n   461→```\n   462→\n   463→## Subprocess Isolation Pattern\n   464→\n   465→For pipelines spawning child Claude sessions, use the 4-layer isolation model:\n   466→\n   467→```python\n   468→def setup_isolation(work_dir: Path) -> dict[str, str]:\n   469→    \"\"\"Create isolated environment for child Claude subprocess.\"\"\"\n   470→    env = os.environ.copy()\n   471→\n   472→    # Layer 1: Scoped work directory\n   473→    env[\"CLAUDE_WORK_DIR\"] = str(work_dir)\n   474→\n   475→    # Layer 2: Git ceiling (prevent escaping work_dir)\n   476→    env[\"GIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES\"] = str(work_dir.parent)\n   477→\n   478→    # Layer 3: Isolated plugin directory\n   479→    plugin_dir = work_dir / \".claude-plugins\"\n   480→    plugin_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)\n   481→    env[\"CLAUDE_PLUGIN_DIR\"] = str(plugin_dir)\n   482→\n   483→    # Layer 4: Isolated settings\n   484→    settings_dir = work_dir / \".claude-settings\"\n   485→    settings_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)\n   486→    env[\"CLAUDE_SETTINGS_DIR\"] = str(settings_dir)\n   487→\n   488→    return env\n   489→```\n   490→\n   491→## Context Injection Pattern\n   492→\n   493→Prior step results feed into subsequent prompts as compressed context:\n   494→\n   495→```python\n   496→def build_step_prompt_with_context(step, prior_results: list[StepResult]) -> str:\n   497→    \"\"\"Build prompt with prior step context injected.\"\"\"\n   498→    base_prompt = step.prompt\n   499→\n   500→    if not prior_results:\n   501→        return base_prompt\n   502→\n   503→    context_block = \"## Prior Step Context\\n\\n\"\n   504→    for result in prior_results[-3:]:  # Keep recent, compress older\n   505→        context_block += result.to_context_summary(verbose=(result == prior_results[-1]))\n   506→        context_block += \"\\n\\n\"\n   507→\n   508→    return f\"{base_prompt}\\n\\n{context_block}\"\n   509→```\n   510→\n   511→## Resume-First Failure Output Pattern\n   512→\n   513→On halt, generate actionable resume information:\n   514→\n   515→```python\n   516→@dataclass\n   517→class MyResult:\n   518→    # ... other fields ...\n   519→\n   520→    def resume_command(self) -> str | None:\n   521→        \"\"\"Generate CLI command to resume from failure point.\"\"\"\n   522→        if not self.halt_step:\n   523→            return None\n   524→        remaining = [r.step.id for r in self.step_results\n   525→                     if r.status == MyStatus.PENDING]\n   526→        return (\n   527→            f\"superclaude {CLI_NAME} run \"\n   528→            f\"--resume --start {self.halt_step} \"\n   529→            f\"--max-turns {self.suggested_resume_budget}\"\n   530→        )\n   531→\n   532→    @property\n   533→    def suggested_resume_budget(self) -> int:\n   534→        \"\"\"Estimate turns needed to complete remaining work.\"\"\"\n   535→        remaining_steps = sum(1 for r in self.step_results\n   536→                              if r.status in (MyStatus.PENDING, MyStatus.INCOMPLETE))\n   537→        return remaining_steps * 25  # Default allocation per step\n   538→```\n   539→\n   540→## Pure-Programmatic Step Execution\n   541→\n   542→Not all steps need Claude. Pure-programmatic steps run as direct Python function calls:\n   543→\n   544→```python\n   545→def execute_step(step, config):\n   546→    \"\"\"Route step to appropriate executor.\"\"\"\n   547→    if step.prompt == \"\":\n   548→        # Call the step's implementation function\n   559→        PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS[step.id](config)\n   560→        return StepResult(step=step, status=StepStatus.PASS,\n   561→                         started_at=started, finished_at=time.time())\n   562→    except Exception as e:\n   563→        return StepResult(step=step, status=StepStatus.FAIL,\n   564→                         gate_failure_reason=str(e),\n   565→                         started_at=started, finished_at=time.time())\n   566→```\n   567→\n   568→## Gate Display State Machine (for TUI)\n   569→\n   570→Model gate states as explicit transitions for richer UX:\n   571→\n   572→```python\n   573→class GateDisplayState(Enum):\n   574→    NONE = \"none\"\n   575→    CHECKING = \"checking\"\n   576→    PASS = \"pass\"\n   577→    FAIL_DEFERRED = \"fail_deferred\"\n   578→    REMEDIATING = \"remediating\"\n   579→    REMEDIATED = \"remediated\"\n   580→    HALT = \"halt\"\n   581→\n   582→    @property\n   583→    def icon(self) -> str:\n   584→        return {\n   585→            \"none\": \" \", \"checking\": \"...\",\n   586→            \"pass\": \"ok\", \"fail_deferred\": \"!\",\n   587→            \"remediating\": \"~\", \"remediated\": \"ok\",\n   588→            \"halt\": \"X\",\n   589→        }[self.value]\n   590→```\n   591→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_014hdZpFbUDh9JzLm2wKNo1V","session_id":"7193c376-0ea5-4fc3-bd2f-4c824eb419dc","uuid":"5a46f57b-c659-4f48-9523-b2da42f96748"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_3p2jLK24gvfqebu0SBo0Qzse","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: sc-cli-portify-protocol\n     3→description: \"Full behavioral protocol for sc:cli-portify — port inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines with sprint-style supervised execution.\"\n     4→category: development\n     5→complexity: high\n     6→allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task\n     7→mcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]\n     8→personas: [architect, analyzer, backend]\n     9→argument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\"\n    10→---\n    11→\n    12→# sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler\n    13→\n    14→Convert inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines that ensure 100% completion and consistency between runs.\n    15→\n    16→## Purpose\n    17→\n    18→SuperClaude workflows implemented as commands + skills + agents + refs rely entirely on Claude's reasoning for orchestration. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n    19→\n    20→- **Deterministic control flow** — Python decides what runs when, not inference\n    21→- **Formal artifact validation** — Gates check output quality programmatically\n    22→- **Resume/retry** — Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n    23→- **Live monitoring** — TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n    24→- **Budget economics** — Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n    25→- **Consistent behavior** — Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n    26→\n    27→The existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n    28→\n    29→## What Gets Generated\n    30→\n    31→A CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n    32→\n    33→| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n    34→|------|---------|----------------|\n    35→| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n    36→| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n    37→| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n    38→| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n    39→| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n    40→| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n    41→| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n    42→| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n    43→| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n    44→| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n    45→| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n    46→| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n    47→| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n    48→| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n    49→\n    50→Plus integration patches for `main.py`.\n    51→\n    52→## Required Input\n    53→\n    54→```\n    55→/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n    56→```\n    57→\n    58→| Argument | Required | Description |\n    59→|----------|----------|-------------|\n    60→| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n    61→| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n    62→| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n    63→| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating code |\n    64→| `--skip-integration` | No | Generate module only, skip main.py wiring |\n    65→\n    66→**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n    67→\n    68→## Behavioral Flow\n    69→\n    70→Four phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n    71→\n    72→### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n    73→\n    74→Load `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n    75→\n    76→**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n    77→\n    78→1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n    79→\n    80→2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n    81→   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n    82→   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n    83→   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n    84→   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n    85→\n    86→3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n    87→   - A new artifact is produced\n    88→   - A different agent takes over\n    89→   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n    90→   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n    91→   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n    92→\n    93→4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n    94→   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n    95→   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n    96→   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n    97→\n    98→5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n    99→\n   100→6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n   101→\n   102→7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n   103→\n   104→**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n   105→\n   106→**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n   107→\n   108→### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n   109→\n   110→Load `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n   111→\n   112→**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n   113→\n   114→1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n   115→\n   116→2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   117→   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   118→   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   119→   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   120→   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   121→   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   122→   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n   123→\n   124→3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   125→   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   126→   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   127→   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   128→   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n   129→\n   130→   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n   131→\n   132→4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   133→   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   134→   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   135→   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n   136→\n   137→5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n   138→\n   139→6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   140→   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   141→   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   142→   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   143→   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   144→   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   145→   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   146→   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   147→   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n   148→\n   149→7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n   150→\n   151→**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n   152→\n   153→**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n   154→\n   155→### Phase 3: Code Generation\n   156→\n   157→Load `refs/code-templates.md` before this phase. It contains parameterized file templates for every module.\n   158→\n   159→Generate files in dependency order (models → gates → prompts → config → monitor → process → executor → tui → logging → diagnostics → commands → __init__). Each file imports from `superclaude.cli.pipeline` for shared base types and follows sprint/roadmap naming conventions.\n   160→\n   161→### Phase 4: Integration\n   162→\n   163→1. Patch `main.py` — Add import and `app.add_command()`\n   164→2. Verify imports — Quick check for circular dependencies\n   165→3. Generate structural test — Validates step graph, gate definitions, and model consistency\n   166→4. Write `portify-summary.md` — File inventory, CLI usage, step graph, known limitations\n   167→\n   168→## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n   169→\n   170→The value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n   171→\n   172→| Operation | Classification | Why |\n   173→|-----------|---------------|-----|\n   174→| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n   175→| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n   176→| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n   177→| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n   178→| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n   179→| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n   180→| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n   181→| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n   182→| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n   183→| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n   184→| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n   185→\n   186→### Rule of Thumb\n   187→If you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n   188→\n   189→## Code Generation Principles\n   190→\n   191→These align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n   192→\n   193→### Critical Constraints\n   194→1. **Synchronous execution** — Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n   195→2. **Gate function signatures** — All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n   196→3. **Runner-authored truth** — Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n   197→4. **Deterministic flow control** — Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n   198→\n   199→### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n   200→5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** — `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n   201→6. **Gate modes** — `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n   202→7. **Turn budget** — `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n   203→8. **Subprocess isolation** — 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n   204→9. **Context injection** — Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n   205→10. **Resume-first failures** — On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n   206→11. **Diagnostic chain** — Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n   207→\n   208→### Output Guidance\n   209→- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. otherwise use `--file` args\n   268→4. **Be explicit about sections** — Name every required section; don't leave structure to inference\n   269→5. **Include depth/focus constraints** — If the step has configurable depth, encode it in the prompt\n   270→\n   271→### Input Embedding Pattern\n   272→\n   273→```python\n   274→def _embed_inputs(prompt: str, inputs: list[Path], config: MyConfig) -> tuple[str, list[str]]:\n   275→    \"\"\"Embed small input files directly into prompt, return file args for large ones.\"\"\"\n   276→    file_args = []\n   277→    for input_path in inputs:\n   278→        full_path = config.work_dir / input_path\n   279→        if full_path.stat().st_size < 50_000:\n   280→            content = full_path.read_text()\n   281→            prompt += f\"\\n\\n---\\n## Input: {input_path}\\n\\n{content}\"\n   282→        else:\n   283→            file_args.append(str(full_path))\n   284→    return prompt, file_args\n   285→```\n   286→\n   287→## Executor Design Patterns\n   288→\n   289→### Sprint-Style Supervisor Loop\n   290→\n   291→The sprint executor pattern provides supervised execution with monitoring. IMPORTANT: Sprint uses synchronous execution with `threading` for parallelism, NOT `async/await`. Use `time.sleep()` polling loops and `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch dispatch.\n   292→\n   293→```python\n   294→def execute_pipeline(config: MyConfig) -> MyResult:\n   295→    # 1. Pre-flight checks\n   296→    verify_claude_binary()\n   297→\n   298→    # 2. Setup infrastructure\n   299→    signal_handler = SignalHandler()\n   300→    logger = MyLogger(config)\n   301→    tui = MyTUI(config)\n   302→    monitor = OutputMonitor()\n   303→    result = MyResult(config=config)\n   304→    ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=config.max_turns)\n   305→\n   306→    # 3. Start TUI\n   307→    tui.start()\n   308→\n   309→    try:\n   310→        for step in config.steps:\n   311→            if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   312→                break\n   313→\n   314→            # 4. Reset monitor for this step\n   315→            monitor.reset(config.output_file(step))\n   316→            monitor.start()\n   317→\n   318→            # 5. Launch Claude subprocess\n   319→            process = ClaudeProcess(config, step)\n   320→            process.start()\n   321→\n   322→            # 6. Supervision loop\n   323→            while process.is_running():\n   324→                if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   325→                    process.stop()\n   326→                    break\n   327→\n   328→                state = monitor.get_state()\n   329→\n   330→                # Stall detection\n   331→                if state.stall_seconds > config.stall_timeout:\n   332→                    process.stop()\n   333→                    break\n   334→\n   335→                # TUI update\n   336→                tui.update(step, state)\n   337→                time.sleep(0.5)\n   338→\n   339→            # 7. Classify result\n   340→            monitor.stop()\n   341→            status = determine_status(process.exit_code, step, config)\n   342→\n   343→            # 8. Record and decide\n   344→            step_result = build_result(step, status, monitor.state)\n   345→            result.add(step_result)\n   346→            logger.write_step_result(step_result)\n   347→\n   348→            if status not in (PASS, PASS_NO_SIGNAL):\n   349→                # Collect diagnostics and halt\n   350→                diagnostics = collect_diagnostics(step_result, monitor.state)\n   351→                write_diagnostic_report(diagnostics, config)\n   352→                result.outcome = HALTED\n   353→                break\n   354→\n   355→    finally:\n   356→        tui.stop()\n   357→        monitor.stop()\n   358→        signal_handler.restore()\n   359→\n   360→    return result\n   361→```\n   362→\n   363→### Status Classification\n   364→\n   365→Map every possible exit condition to a deterministic status:\n   366→\n   367→```python\n   368→def determine_status(exit_code, step, config):\n   369→    # 1. Hard failures\n   370→    if exit_code == 124:\n   371→        return TIMEOUT\n   372→    if exit_code != 0:\n   373→        return ERROR\n   374→\n   375→    # 2. Check for structured result file\n   376→    result_path = config.result_file(step)\n   377→    if result_path.exists():\n   378→        content = result_path.read_text()\n   379→        if \"EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: HALT\" in content:\n   380→            return HALT\n   381→        if \"EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE\" in content:\n   382→            return PASS\n   383→        return PASS_NO_SIGNAL\n   384→\n   385→    # 3. Check for output without result\n   386→    output_path = config.output_file(step)\n   387→    if output_path.exists():\n   388→        if detect_error_max_turns(output_path):\n   389→            return INCOMPLETE\n   390→        return PASS_NO_REPORT\n   391→\n   392→    # 4. No output at all\n   393→    return ERROR\n   394→```\n   395→\n   396→## Integration Patterns\n   397→\n   398→### main.py Registration\n   399→\n   400→```python\n   401→# In 430→For pipelines with multiple Claude subprocesses, use `TurnLedger` to manage budget:\n   431→\n   432→```python\n   433→from superclaude.cli.sprint.models import TurnLedger\n   434→\n   435→@dataclass\n   436→class MyConfig(PipelineConfig):\n   437→    max_turns: int = 200\n   438→    min_launch_allocation: int = 10\n   439→    min_remediation_budget: int = 5\n   440→\n   441→# In setup_isolation(work_dir: Path) -> dict[str, str]:\n   469→    \"\"\"Create isolated environment for child Claude subprocess.\"\"\"\n   470→    env = os.environ.copy()\n   471→\n   472→    # Layer 1: 493→Prior step results feed into subsequent prompts as compressed context:\n   494→\n   495→```python\n   496→def build_step_prompt_with_context(step, prior_results: list[StepResult]) -> str:\n   497→    \"\"\"Build prompt with prior step context injected.\"\"\"\n   498→    base_prompt = step.prompt\n   499→\n   500→    if not prior_results:\n   501→        return base_prompt\n   502→\n   503→ == prior_results[-1]))\n   506→        context_block += \"\\n\\n\"\n   507→\n   508→    return f\"{base_prompt}\\n\\n{context_block}\"\n   509→```\n   510→\n   511→## Resume-First Failure Output Pattern\n   512→\n   513→On halt, generate actionable resume information:\n   514→\n   515→```python\n   516→@dataclass\n   517→class MyResult:\n   518→    # ... other fields ...\n   519→\n   520→      remaining = [r.step.id for r in self.step_results\n   525→                     if r.status == MyStatus.PENDING]\n   526→        return (\n   527→            f\"superclaude {CLI_NAME} run \"\n   528→            f\"--resume --start {self.halt_step} \"\n   529→            f\"--max-turns {self.suggested_resume_budget}\"\n   530→        )\n   531→\n   532→    @property\n   533→    def                     if r.status in (MyStatus.PENDING, MyStatus.INCOMPLETE))\n   537→        return remaining_steps * 25  # Default allocation per step\n   538→```\n   539→\n   540→## Pure-Programmatic Step Execution\n   541→\n   542→Not all steps need Claude. What the roadmap says overall\n\nRoadmap file:\n- `/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/.dev/releases/current/v2.18-cli-portify-v2/roadmap.md`\n\n### Overall intent\nThe roadmap describes refactoring `sc-cli-portify` from a monolithic skill into a command/protocol split architecture with:\n- contract-driven phase boundaries\n- live API conformance checks\n- deterministic code generation\n- AST verification\n- resumable failures\n- explicit supported-pattern boundaries\n\nIt frames the work as a 5-phase portification pipeline.\n\n### Phase breakdown from the roadmap\n#### Phase 1: Foundation and prerequisite remediation\nMain goals:\n- fix stale refs against live API\n- create `sc-cli-portify-protocol`\n- create `src/superclaude/commands/cli-portify.md`\n- promote YAML frontmatter\n- deprecate old `sc-cli-portify`\n- resolve 10 open questions\n\n#### Phase 2: Contract infrastructure, Phase 0 and Phase 1\nMain goals:\n- define versioned YAML contracts\n- implement contract validation and resume protocol\n- Phase 0 prerequisite scanning\n- Phase 1 workflow analysis\n- TodoWrite integration\n\n#### Phase 3: Protocol core design\nMain goals:\n- step mapping / coverage invariant\n- model and gate design\n- prompt and executor design\n- emit `portify-spec.yaml`\n\n#### Phase 4: Code generation and integration\nMain goals:\n- generate 12 Python files\n- validate per-file and cross-file correctness\n- patch `main.py`\n- generate structural tests\n- generate `portify-summary.md`\n- emit integration contract\n\n#### Phase 5: Validation, testing, {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_3uUZKTNkL0dwMH4ZGxYMFZyF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# D-0010: Contract Schema Versioning Policy\n     2→\n     3→**Task**: T02.01\n     4→**Roadmap Items**: R-018, R-019, R-020, R-026\n     5→**Date**: 2026-03-08\n     6→\n     7→## Schema Version Format\n     8→\n     9→All portify contracts use semantic versioning in the `schema_version` field:\n    10→\n    11→```\n    12→schema_version: \"1.0\"\n    13→```\n    14→\n    15→**Format**: `MAJOR.MINOR` (string, quoted)\n    16→- **MAJOR**: Incremented on breaking changes (field removal, type change, semantic redefinition)\n    17→- **MINOR**: Incremented on additive changes (new optional fields)\n    18→\n    19→## Backward-Compatibility Rules\n    20→\n    21→| Change Type | Allowed? | Version Impact |\n    22→|-------------|----------|----------------|\n    23→| Add new optional field | Yes | Minor bump |\n    24→| Add new required field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    25→| Remove field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    26→| Change field type | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    27→| Change allowed enum values (additive) | Yes | Minor bump |\n    28→| Remove enum value | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    29→| Rename field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    30→\n    31→## Version Validation on Contract Read\n    32→\n    33→When a phase reads an incoming contract:\n    34→\n    35→1. Parse `schema_version` field\n    36→2. Extract `MAJOR.MINOR` components\n    37→3. Validate compatibility:\n    38→   - **Same MAJOR, same or lower MINOR**: Compatible — proceed\n    39→   - **Higher MINOR**: Compatible (additive fields ignored by older consumer) — proceed with advisory warning\n    40→   - **Different MAJOR**: Incompatible — abort with actionable error\n    41→\n    42→**Error format on incompatible version**:\n    43→\n    44→```\n    45→CONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH: Expected schema_version 1.x, got 2.0.\n    46→Phase {N} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version.\n    47→Action: Re-run Phase {N-1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\n    48→```\n    49→\n    50→## Common Header Schema\n    51→\n    52→Every portify contract includes this common header:\n    53→\n    54→```yaml\n    55→schema_version: \"1.0\"          # String. Required. Format: \"MAJOR.MINOR\"\n    56→phase: <int>                    # Integer 0-4. Required. Producing phase number.\n    57→status: <enum>                  # String. Required. One of: \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\"\n    58→timestamp: <ISO8601>            # String. Required. UTC ISO 8601 datetime.\n    59→resume_checkpoint: <string>     # String. Required. Identifier for resume point.\n    60→                                # Format: \"phase-{N}:{step}\" e.g. \"phase-0:collision-check\"\n    61→validation_status:              # Object. Required.\n    62→  blocking_passed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that passed.\n    63→  blocking_failed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that failed.\n    64→  advisory: <list[string]>      # List of strings. Advisory warnings (non-blocking).\n    65→```\n    66→\n    67→**Field Type Summary**:\n    68→\n    69→| Field | Type | Required | Allowed Values |\n    70→|-------|------|----------|----------------|\n    71→| `schema_version` | string | Yes | Semantic version \"MAJOR.MINOR\" |\n    72→| `phase` | integer | Yes | 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 |\n    73→| `status` | string | Yes | \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\" |\n    74→| `timestamp` | string | Yes | ISO 8601 UTC datetime |\n    75→| `resume_checkpoint` | string | Yes | \"phase-{N}:{step}\" |\n    76→| `validation_status` | object | Yes | See sub-fields |\n    77→| `validation_status.blocking_passed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n    78→| `validation_status.blocking_failed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n    79→| `validation_status.advisory` | list[string] | Yes | Free-form advisory messages |\n    80→\n    81→## Null-Field Policy\n    82→\n    83→Fields for unreached phases or inapplicable data are explicitly set to `null`, never omitted.\n    84→\n    85→**Rules**:\n    86→1. All fields defined in a contract schema MUST be present in the emitted YAML\n    87→2. Unreached or inapplicable fields are set to `null`\n    88→3. Empty lists are represented as `[]`, not `null`\n    89→4. Empty objects are represented as `{}`, not `null`\n    90→5. A consumer reading a contract can distinguish \"not yet computed\" (`null`) from \"computed and empty\" (`[]` / `{}`)\n    91→\n    92→**Example — Phase 0 contract emitted before Phase 1 runs**:\n    93→\n    94→```yaml\n    95→schema_version: \"1.0\"\n    96→phase: 0\n    97→status: \"passed\"\n    98→timestamp: \"2026-03-08T14:30:00Z\"\n    99→resume_checkpoint: \"phase-0:complete\"\n   100→validation_status:\n   101→  blocking_passed: 3\n   102→  blocking_failed: 0\n   103→  advisory: []\n   104→# Phase 0 specific fields populated:\n   105→workflow_path: \"src/superclaude/skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/\"\n   106→api_snapshot_hash: \"sha256:abc123...\"\n   107→collision_status: \"clean\"\n   108→pattern_scan_result: \"supported\"\n   109→# Phase 1+ fields not yet populated:\n   110→component_inventory: null\n   111→step_graph: null\n   112→```\n   113→\n   114→## Contract File Naming Convention\n   115→\n   116→| Phase | Contract File | Producer | Consumer |\n   117→|-------|--------------|----------|----------|\n   118→| 0 | `portify-prerequisites.yaml` | Phase 0 | Phase 1 |\n   119→| 1 | `portify-analysis.yaml` | Phase 1 | Phase 2 |\n   120→| 2 | `portify-spec.yaml` | Phase 2 | Phase 3 |\n   121→| 3 | `portify-codegen.yaml` | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |\n   122→| 4 | `portify-integration.yaml` | Phase 4 | Return contract |\n   123→| Return | embedded in return contract | Phase 5 / aggregator | Caller |\n   124→\n   125→## Schema Version History\n   126→\n   127→| Version | Date | Changes |\n   128→|---------|------|---------|\n   129→| 1.0 | 2026-03-08 | Initial schema definition |\n   130→\n   131→## References\n   132→\n   133→- OQ-004: Integration schema resolution (decisions.yaml)\n   134→- OQ-007: Approval gate mechanism resolution (decisions.yaml)\n   135→- Roadmap M2.1: Contract Infrastructure and Schema Versioning\n No spec change needed.\n\n### OQ-003: --dry-run behavior\n- **Status**: Resolved (Blocking)\n- **Resolution**: `--dry-run` = execute Phases 0-2 only. Emit contracts (`portify-prerequisites.yaml`, `portify-analysis.yaml`), display analysis to user. No code generation (Phase 3) or integration (Phase 4). `--skip-integration` = generate code (Phase 3) but skip `main.py` wiring (Phase 4).\n\n### OQ-004: Integration schema\n- **Status**: Resolved (Blocking)\n- **Resolution**: `portify-integration.yaml` schema:\n  ```yaml\n  schema_version: \"1.0\"\n  phase: 4\n  status: \"passed\" | \"failed\"\n  timestamp: <ISO8601>\n  main_py_patched: true | false\n  command_registered: true | false\n  test_file_generated: true | false\n  smoke_test_passed: true | false\n  ```\n\n### OQ-005: batch_dynamic\n- **Status**: Resolved (Non-blocking)\n- **Resolution**: Set `batch_dynamic: false` always. File exists at `src/superclaude/skills/sc-cli-portify/refs/analysis-protocol.md` (216 lines). Write contract artifact to disk\n  2. Mark TodoWrite task as \"awaiting review\"\n  3. Present summary to user with key decisions\n  4. User resumes by continuing (implicit approval) or provides overrides\n  5. Protocol reads contract on resume and validates completed phases\n\n### OQ-008: Default output path\n- **Status**: Resolved (Blocking)\n- **Resolution**: Default `--output` to `src/superclaude/cli/<derived_name>/` where `<derived_name>` is the kebab-case CLI name with `sc-` prefix and `-protocol` suffix stripped. This affects contract emission paths — all contracts are written to the output directory.\n\n### OQ-009: Test file location\n- **Status**: Resolved (Non-blocking)\n- **Resolution**: Structural tests go to `tests/` per project convention. File named `test_<cli_name>_structure.py`. This follows the existing project pattern where all tests reside in the `tests/` directory.\n\n### OQ-010: Step boundary algorithm\n- **Status**: Resolved (Blocking for Phase 3)\n- **Resolution**: The step boundary algorithm is already documented in `refs/analysis-protocol.md` under \"## Step Decomposition Algorithm\" → \"### Identify Step Boundaries\". The algorithm states a new Step starts when:\n  - A new artifact is produced\n  - A different agent takes over\n  - The execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n  - A quality gate must be evaluated\n  - The operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\n  No additional extraction needed — the algorithm is already explicitly documented.\n\n## Summary\n\n| OQ | Blocking? | Status |\n|----|-----------|--------|\n| OQ-001 | No | Resolved |\n| OQ-002 | Yes | Resolved — TurnLedger not in pipeline API |\n| OQ-003 | Yes | Resolved — dry-run = Phases 0-2 only |\n| OQ-004 | Yes | Resolved — schema defined |\n| OQ-005 | No | Resolved — batch_dynamic removed |\n| OQ-006 | No | Resolved — file confirmed |\n| OQ-007 | Yes | Resolved — TodoWrite checkpoint pattern |\n| OQ-008 | Yes | Resolved — default src/superclaude/cli/<name>/ |\n| OQ-009 | No | Resolved — tests/ directory |\n| OQ-010 | Yes | Resolved — already in analysis-protocol.md |\n\n**All 10 OQs resolved. | Version Impact |\n|-------------|----------|----------------|\n| Add new optional field | Yes | Minor bump |\n| Add new required field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Remove field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Change field type | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Change allowed enum values (additive) | Yes | Minor bump |\n| Remove enum value | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Rename field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n\n## Version Validation on Contract Read\n\nWhen a phase reads an incoming contract:\n\n1. Parse `schema_version` field\n2. Extract `MAJOR.MINOR` components\n3. Validate compatibility:\n   - **Same MAJOR, same or lower MINOR**: Compatible — proceed\n   - **Higher MINOR**: Compatible (additive fields ignored by older consumer) — proceed with advisory warning\n   - **Different MAJOR**: Incompatible — abort with actionable error\n\n**Error format on incompatible version**:\n\n```\nCONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH: Expected schema_version 1.x, got 2.0.\nPhase {N} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version.\nAction: Re-run Phase {N-1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\n```\n\n## Common Header Schema\n\nEvery portify contract includes this common header:\n\n```yaml\nschema_version: \"1.0\"          # String. Required. Format: \"MAJOR.MINOR\"\nphase: <int>                    # Integer 0-4. Required. Producing phase number.\nstatus: <enum>                  # String. Required. One of: \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\"\ntimestamp: <ISO8601>            # String. Required. UTC ISO 8601 datetime.\nresume_checkpoint: <string>     # String. Required. Identifier for resume point.\n                                # Format: \"phase-{N}:{step}\" e.g. \"phase-0:collision-check\"\nvalidation_status:              # Object. Required.\n  blocking_passed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that passed.\n  blocking_failed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that failed.\n  advisory: <list[string]>      # List of strings. Advisory warnings (non-blocking).\n```\n\n**Field Type Summary**:\n\n| Field | Type | Required | Allowed Values |\n|-------|------|----------|----------------|\n| `schema_version` | string | Yes | Semantic version \"MAJOR.MINOR\" |\n| `phase` | integer | Yes | 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 |\n| `status` | string | Yes | \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\" |\n| `timestamp` | string | Yes | ISO 8601 UTC datetime |\n| `resume_checkpoint` | string | Yes | \"phase-{N}:{step}\" |\n| `validation_status` | object | Yes | See sub-fields |\n| `validation_status.blocking_passed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n| `validation_status.blocking_failed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n| `validation_status.advisory` | list[string] | Yes | Free-form advisory messages |\n\n## Null-Field Policy\n\nFields for unreached phases or inapplicable data are explicitly set to `null`, never omitted.\n\n**Rules**:\n1. All fields defined in a contract schema MUST be present in the emitted YAML\n2. Unreached or inapplicable fields are set to `null`\n3. Empty lists are represented as `[]`, not `null`\n4. Empty objects are represented as `{}`, not `null`\n5. A consumer reading a contract can distinguish \"not yet computed\" (`null`) from \"computed and empty\" (`[]` / `{}`)\n\n**Example — Phase 0 contract emitted before Phase 1 runs**:\n\n```yaml\nschema_version: \"1.0\"\nphase: 0\nstatus: \"passed\"\ntimestamp: \"2026-03-08T14:30:00Z\"\nresume_checkpoint: \"phase-0:complete\"\nvalidation_status:\n  blocking_passed: 3\n  blocking_failed: 0\n  advisory: []\n# Phase 0 specific fields populated:\nworkflow_path: \"src/superclaude/skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/\"\napi_snapshot_hash: \"sha256:abc123...\"\ncollision_status: \"clean\"\npattern_scan_result: \"supported\"\n# Phase 1+ fields not yet populated:\ncomponent_inventory: null\nstep_graph: null\n```\n\n## Contract File Naming Convention\n\n| Phase | Contract File | Producer | Consumer |\n|-------|--------------|----------|----------|\n| 0 | `portify-prerequisites.yaml` | Phase 0 | Phase 1 |\n| 1 | `portify-analysis.yaml` | Phase 1 | Phase 2 |\n| 2 | `portify-spec.yaml` | Phase 2 | Phase 3 |\n| 3 | `portify-codegen.yaml` | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |\n| 4 | `portify-integration.yaml` | Phase 4 | Return contract |\n| Return | embedded in return contract | Phase 5 / aggregator | Caller |\n\n## Schema Version History\n\n| Version | Date | Changes |\n|---------|------|---------|\n| 1.0 | 2026-03-08 | Initial schema definition |\n\n## References\n\n- OQ-004: Integration schema resolution (decisions.yaml)\n- OQ-007: Approval gate mechanism resolution (decisions.yaml)\n- Roadmap M2.1: Contract Infrastructure and Schema Versioning\n```\n\n4. `/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/.dev/releases/current/v2.18-cli-portify-v2/artifacts/D-0011/spec.md`\n\n```md\n# D-0011: Per-Phase Contract Schemas\n\n**Task**: | Version Impact |\n|-------------|----------|----------------|\n| Add new optional field | Yes | Minor bump |\n| Add new required field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Remove field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Change field type | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Change allowed enum values (additive) | Yes | Minor bump |\n| Remove enum value | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n| Rename field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n\n## Version Validation on Contract Read\n\nWhen a phase reads an incoming contract:\n\n1. Parse `schema_version` field\n2. Extract `MAJOR.MINOR` components\n3. Validate compatibility:\n   - **Same MAJOR, same or lower MINOR**: Compatible — proceed\n   - **Higher MINOR**: Compatible (additive fields ignored by older consumer) — proceed with advisory warning\n   - **Different MAJOR**: Incompatible — abort with actionable error\n\n**Error format on incompatible version**:\n\n```\nCONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH: Expected schema_version 1.x, got 2.0.\nPhase {N} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version.\nAction: Re-run Phase {N-1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\n```\n\n## Common Header Schema\n\nEvery portify contract includes this common header:\n\n```yaml\nschema_version: \"1.0\"          # String. Required. Format: \"MAJOR.MINOR\"\nphase: <int>                    # Integer 0-4. Required. Producing phase number.\nstatus: <enum>                  # String. Required. One of: \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\"\ntimestamp: <ISO8601>            # String. Required. UTC ISO 8601 datetime.\nresume_checkpoint: <string>     # String. Required. Identifier for resume point.\n                                # Format: \"phase-{N}:{step}\" e.g. \"phase-0:collision-check\"\nvalidation_status:              # Object. Required.\n  blocking_passed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that passed.\n  blocking_failed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that failed.\n  advisory: <list[string]>      # List of strings. Advisory warnings (non-blocking).\n```\n\n**Field Type Summary**:\n\n| Field | Type | Required | Allowed Values |\n|-------|------|----------|----------------|\n| `schema_version` | string | Yes | Semantic version \"MAJOR.MINOR\" |\n| `phase` | integer | Yes | 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 |\n| `status` | string | Yes | \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\" |\n| `timestamp` | string | Yes | ISO 8601 UTC datetime |\n| `resume_checkpoint` | string | Yes | \"phase-{N}:{step}\" |\n| `validation_status` | object | Yes | See sub-fields |\n| `validation_status.blocking_passed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n| `validation_status.blocking_failed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n| `validation_status.advisory` | list[string] | Yes | Free-form advisory messages |\n\n## Null-Field Policy\n\nFields for unreached phases or inapplicable data are explicitly set to `null`, never omitted.\n\n**Rules**:\n1. All fields defined in a contract schema MUST be present in the emitted YAML\n2. Unreached or inapplicable fields are set to `null`\n3. Empty lists are represented as `[]`, not `null`\n4. Empty objects are represented as `{}`, not `null`\n5. A consumer reading a contract can distinguish \"not yet computed\" (`null`) from \"computed and empty\" (`[]` / `{}`)\n\n**Example — Phase 0 contract emitted before Phase 1 runs**:\n\n```yaml\nschema_version: \"1.0\"\nphase: 0\nstatus: \"passed\"\ntimestamp: \"2026-03-08T14:30:00Z\"\nresume_checkpoint: \"phase-0:complete\"\nvalidation_status:\n  blocking_passed: 3\n  blocking_failed: 0\n  advisory: []\n# Phase 0 specific fields populated:\nworkflow_path: \"src/superclaude/skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/\"\napi_snapshot_hash: \"sha256:abc123...\"\ncollision_status: \"clean\"\npattern_scan_result: \"supported\"\n# Phase 1+ fields not yet populated:\ncomponent_inventory: null\nstep_graph: null\n```\n\n## Contract File Naming Convention\n\n| Phase | Contract File | Producer | Consumer |\n|-------|--------------|----------|----------|\n| 0 | `portify-prerequisites.yaml` | Phase 0 | Phase 1 |\n| 1 | `portify-analysis.yaml` | Phase 1 | Phase 2 |\n| 2 | `portify-spec.yaml` | Phase 2 | Phase 3 |\n| 3 | `portify-codegen.yaml` | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |\n| 4 | `portify-integration.yaml` | Phase 4 | Return contract |\n| Return | embedded in return contract | Phase 5 / aggregator | Caller |\n\n## Schema Version History\n\n| Version | Date | Changes |\n|---------|------|---------|\n| 1.0 | 2026-03-08 | Initial schema definition |\n\n## References\n\n- OQ-004: Integration schema resolution (decisions.yaml)\n- OQ-007: Approval gate mechanism resolution (decisions.yaml)\n- Roadmap M2.1: Contract Infrastructure and Schema Versioning\n```\n\n4. `/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/.dev/releases/current/v2.18-cli-portify-v2/artifacts/D-0011/spec.md`\n\n```md\n# D-0011: Per-Phase Contract Schemas\n\n**Task**: Contract Validation Logic\n\n### Interface\n\n```\nvalidate_contract(contract_path: str, expected_phase: int) -> ValidatedContract | ContractError\n```\n\n### Validation Steps\n\nOn reading an incoming contract, the validator performs these checks in order:\n\n#### Step 1: File Existence and Parse\n- Verify file exists at `contract_path`\n- Parse YAML content\n- On parse failure: return `ContractError(\"YAML_PARSE_FAILED\", path, details)`\n\n#### Step 2: Common Header Validation\n- Verify `schema_version` field exists and is a string matching `\"MAJOR.MINOR\"` pattern\n- Verify `phase` field exists and equals `expected_phase - Same MAJOR, any MINOR: **compatible** (proceed)\n  - Different MAJOR: **incompatible** (abort)\n- On incompatible version:\n  ```\n  ContractError(\n    code=\"CONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH\",\n    message=\"Expected schema_version 1.x, got {actual}. \"\n            \"Phase {expected_phase - 1} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version. \"\n            \"Action: Re-run Phase {expected_phase - 1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\"\n  )\n  ```\n\n#### Step 4: Required Field Presence (Phase-Specific)\n- Load the expected field set for the contract's phase from the schema registry (D-0011)\n- For each required field:\n  - Verify field key exists in parsed YAML\n  - `null` values are allowed (per null-field policy from D-0010)\n  - Missing keys are NOT allowed\n- On missing required fields:\n  ```\n  ContractError(\n    code=\"MISSING_REQUIRED_FIELDS\",\n    message=\"Contract at {path} is missing required fields: {missing_fields}. \"\n            \"Action: Re-run Phase {phase} to regenerate the contract.\"\n  )\n  ```\n\n#### Step 5: Status Enum Validation\n- Verify `status` is one of the allowed values: `\"passed\"`, `\"failed\"`, `\"skipped\"`\n- Verify `phase` is in range 0-4 (or -1 for return contract)\n\n#### Step 6: Blocking Failure Check\n- If `status == \"failed\"` AND `validation_status.blocking_failed > 0`:\n  - Return validated contract with `can_proceed = False`\n  - Include failure details for downstream decision-making\n\n### Output\n\n```\nValidatedContract:\n  data: dict              # Parsed and validated contract data\n  schema_version: str     # Parsed version\n  phase: int              # Producing phase\n  status: str             # \"passed\" | \"failed\" | \"skipped\"\n  can_proceed: bool       # True if consuming phase should proceed\n  warnings: list[str]     # Advisory warnings (e.g., higher minor version)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Return Contract Assembly\n\n### Interface\n\n```\nassemble_return_contract(phase_contracts: dict[int, ValidatedContract], pipeline_state: PipelineState) -> dict\n```\n\n### Assembly Logic\n\n1. **Determine overall status**:\n   - If all phases passed: `status = \"passed\"`\n   - If any phase failed: `status = \"failed\"`\n   - If pipeline was halted before completion: `status = \"failed\"`\n\n2. **Identify failure information**:\n   - `failure_phase`: Phase number where first failure occurred, `null` if passed\n   - `failure_type`: Classification of failure, `null` if passed\n     - `\"validation_failed\"`: Self-validation check failed\n     - `\"gate_failed\"`: Gate validation failed\n     - `\"unsupported_pattern\"`: Phase 0 detected unsupported pattern\n     - `\"collision\"`: Output directory collision detected\n     - `\"generation_error\"`: Code generation failed\n     - `hybrid_steps`: Count where `classification == \"hybrid\"`\n   - `files_generated`: From Phase 3 `generated_files` length\n   - `gates_passed` / `gates_failed`: From Phase 3 validation results\n\n5. **Populate remaining fields**:\n   - `api_snapshot_hash`: From Phase 0 `api_snapshot.content_hash`\n   - `resume_command`: Generated from failure point if failed, `null` if passed\n   - `warnings`: Aggregated from all `validation_status.advisory` lists\n   -
